### Section: 11.1 Introduction to Civil Engineering Hydraulics:

Hydraulics is a fundamental aspect of civil engineering, dealing with the study and application of fluid mechanics to the design and analysis of hydraulic systems. It is a branch of fluid mechanics that deals with the study of fluids in motion, particularly water and its effects on man-made structures such as dams, bridges, and canals.

#### 11.1a Basics of Hydraulics

Hydraulics is governed by the principles of fluid mechanics, which is the study of how fluids (liquids, gases, and plasmas) move. The behavior of fluids is described by the Navier-Stokes equations, which are a set of nonlinear partial differential equations that describe the motion of viscous fluid substances.

The fundamental principles of hydraulics include fluid mechanics, fluid flow, behavior of real fluids, hydrology, pipelines, open channel hydraulics, mechanics of sediment transport, physical modeling, hydraulic machines, and drainage hydraulics.

#### Fluid Mechanics

Fluid mechanics is the study of fluids at rest, known as hydrostatics, and fluids in motion, known as hydrodynamics. Hydrostatics deals with the study of fluids at rest, where the pressure at any point in the fluid is the same in all directions. This is described by the equation:

$$
\frac{dP}{dz} = -\rho g
$$

where $P$ is pressure, $z$ is height, $\rho$ is density, and $g$ is acceleration due to gravity.

Hydrodynamics, on the other hand, deals with the study of fluids in motion. This is described by the Navier-Stokes equations, which describe the motion of viscous fluid substances.

#### Behavior of Real Fluids

Real fluids, unlike ideal fluids, have viscosity and do not follow the principles of ideal fluid flow. Viscous flow refers to the deformation of a fluid under a shear force, as described by Pascal's law. Ideal fluid, on the other hand, does not deform and follows Bernoulli's equation along streamlines.

#### Viscous Flow

Viscous flow can be classified into stable, transition, and unstable flows, depending on the effects of disturbance on the flow.

#### Bernoulli's Equation

Bernoulli's equation is a fundamental principle in fluid mechanics that describes the conservation of energy principle for flowing fluids. It states that the sum of the kinetic energy, potential energy, and pressure energy in a fluid system remains constant along a streamline. This equation is often used in the design and analysis of hydraulic systems.

In the next section, we will delve deeper into the applications of hydraulics in civil engineering, including the design of hydraulic systems, the analysis of hydraulic structures, and the prediction of flood and wave effects.

#### 11.1b Applications of Hydraulics

Hydraulics has a wide range of applications in civil engineering. It is used in the design and analysis of various structures and systems, including dams, bridges, canals, and hydraulic machines. Hydraulics is also used in the prediction of flood and wave effects, and in the design of drainage systems.

#### Dams

Hydraulics plays a crucial role in the design and analysis of dams. The behavior of water under pressure, the effects of sediment transport, and the design of spillways and outlet works are all governed by the principles of hydraulics. For example, the ASME PTC 12.1 Feedwater Heater Standard is a widely used code for the procedures, direction, and guidance for determining the thermo-hydraulic performance of a closed feedwater heater.

#### Bridges

In the design of bridges, hydraulics is used to analyze the effects of water flow on the bridge structure. This includes the prediction of scour and the design of scour protection measures. Hydraulics is also used in the design of hydraulic jumps, which are used to dissipate energy in high-head hydraulic structures.

#### Canals

Hydraulics is used in the design and analysis of canals, including the design of locks and the prediction of flow rates and water levels. The principles of hydraulics are also used in the design of hydraulic machines, such as pumps and turbines.

#### Flood and Wave Effects

Hydraulics is used in the prediction of flood and wave effects, which are crucial in the design of flood protection measures and coastal structures. The principles of hydraulics are also used in the design of drainage systems, including the design of pipes and culverts.

#### Hydraulic Machines

Hydraulic machines, such as pumps and turbines, are used in a variety of applications in civil engineering. The design and analysis of these machines are governed by the principles of hydraulics.

In conclusion, hydraulics is a fundamental aspect of civil engineering, with a wide range of applications in the design and analysis of various structures and systems. The principles of hydraulics are used to predict the behavior of water under various conditions, to design and analyze structures, and to design and analyze hydraulic machines.

#### 11.1c Case Studies in Hydraulics

In this section, we will explore some case studies that illustrate the application of hydraulics in civil engineering. These case studies will provide a practical perspective on the principles and concepts discussed in the previous sections.

##### Case Study 1: Blue Hill Hydraulics and the Alewife Migration

Blue Hill Hydraulics, a civil engineering firm, used the FLOW-3D software to update the design of a fish ladder on Mt. Desert Island, Maine, that helps alewife migrate to the fresh water spawning habitat. The FLOW-3D simulation demonstrated that the existing energy dissipation structure was not capable of handling the maximum expected overflow rate. The problem was solved by increasing the height of the wing walls by exactly one foot. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

##### Case Study 2: AECOM Technology Corporation and the Powell Butte Reservoir

AECOM Technology Corporation studied emergency overflows from the Powell Butte Reservoir and demonstrated that the existing energy dissipation structure was not capable of handling the maximum expected overflow rate. The FLOW-3D simulation predicted that the problem could be solved by increasing the height of the wing walls by exactly one foot. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

##### Case Study 3: Researchers from the CAST Cooperative Research Centre and M. Murray Associates

Researchers from the CAST Cooperative Research Centre and M. Murray Associates developed flow and thermal control methods for the high pressure die casting of thin-walled aluminum components with thicknesses of less than 1 mm. FLOW-3D simulation predicted the complex structure of the metal flow in the die and subsequent casting solidification. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

##### Case Study 4: Researchers at DuPont

Researchers at DuPont used FLOW-3D to optimize coating processes for a solution-coated active-matrix organic light-emitting diode (AMOLED) display technology. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

##### Case Study 5: Eastman Kodak Company

Eastman Kodak Company researchers rapidly developed an inkjet printer technology using FLOW 3-D simulation technology for predicting the performance of printhead designs. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

##### Case Study 6: Auburn University, Lamar University and RJR Engineering

A research team composed of members from Auburn University, Lamar University and RJR Engineering used Flow Science’s TruVOF method as a virtual laboratory to evaluate performance of highway pavement and drainage inlets with different geometries. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

##### Case Study 7: Albany Chicago LLC and the University of Wisconsin – Milwaukee

A research team composed of members from Albany Chicago LLC and the University of Wisconsin – Milwaukee used FLOW-3D in conjunction with a one-dimensional algorithm to analyze the slow-shot and fast-shot die casting processes. This case study illustrates the use of hydraulic simulations in the design and analysis of civil engineering structures.

These case studies provide a practical perspective on the principles and concepts discussed in the previous sections. They illustrate the wide range of applications of hydraulics in civil engineering, from the design of hydraulic structures to the optimization of coating processes.

Calculate the flow rate of a fluid with a velocity of 2 m/s and a cross-sectional area of 0.5 m².

#### Exercise 2
A dam is designed to withstand a maximum water pressure of 100 kPa. If the dam is 20 m high, what is the maximum allowable water depth?

#### Exercise 3
A bridge is designed to support a maximum load of 500 kN. If the bridge is 10 m long, what is the maximum allowable load per meter?

#### Exercise 4

#### Exercise 5
A hydraulic turbine is designed to generate electricity at a rate of 100 kW. If the turbine operates at a head of 100 m and a flow rate of 0.5 m³/s, what is the efficiency of the turbine?

### Section: 11.2 Fluid Mechanics:

Fluid mechanics is a fundamental aspect of civil engineering, dealing with the study and application of fluid mechanics to the design and analysis of hydraulic systems. It is a branch of fluid mechanics that deals with the study of fluids in motion, particularly water and its effects on man-made structures such as dams, bridges, and canals.

#### 11.2a Introduction to Fluid Mechanics

Fluid mechanics is governed by the principles of fluid dynamics, which is the study of how fluids move. The behavior of fluids is described by the Navier-Stokes equations, which are a set of nonlinear partial differential equations that describe the motion of viscous fluid substances.

The fundamental principles of fluid mechanics include fluid dynamics, fluid flow, behavior of real fluids, hydrology, pipelines, open channel hydraulics, mechanics of sediment transport, physical modeling, hydraulic machines, and drainage hydraulics.

#### Fluid Dynamics

Fluid dynamics is the study of fluids in motion. It deals with the forces that cause fluid motion and the resulting motion itself. The Navier-Stokes equations, which describe the motion of viscous fluid substances, are fundamental to the study of fluid dynamics.

#### Fluid Flow

Fluid flow refers to the movement of fluids. It can be classified into two types: laminar and turbulent. Laminar flow is smooth and orderly, while turbulent flow is chaotic and disordered. The type of flow can greatly affect the design and operation of hydraulic systems.

#### Behavior of Real Fluids

Real fluids, unlike ideal fluids, have viscosity and do not follow the principles of ideal fluid flow. Viscous flow refers to the deformation of a fluid under a shear force, as described by Pascal's law. Ideal fluid, on the other hand, does not deform and follows Bernoulli's equation along streamlines.

#### Viscous Flow

Viscous flow can be classified into two types: laminar and turbulent. Laminar flow is smooth and orderly, while turbulent flow is chaotic and disordered. The type of flow can greatly affect the design and operation of hydraulic systems.

#### Hydrology

Hydrology is the study of the movement, distribution, and quality of water throughout the Earth. It is a crucial aspect of fluid mechanics, as it deals with the behavior of water, which is the most common fluid encountered in civil engineering.

#### Pipelines

Pipelines are a common component of hydraulic systems. They are used to transport fluids over long distances. The design and operation of pipelines are governed by the principles of fluid mechanics, particularly fluid dynamics and fluid flow.

#### Open Channel Hydraulics

Open channel hydraulics deals with the study of fluid flow in open channels, such as rivers and canals. It is a crucial aspect of civil engineering, as it deals with the behavior of water in natural and man-made channels.

#### Mechanics of Sediment Transport

The mechanics of sediment transport deals with the movement of sediment in fluid flow. It is a crucial aspect of civil engineering, as it deals with the behavior of sediment in rivers and other water bodies.

#### Physical Modeling

Physical modeling is the process of creating a physical model of a hydraulic system to study its behavior. It is a powerful tool in the study of fluid mechanics, as it allows for the visualization and analysis of complex fluid flow phenomena.

#### Hydraulic Machines

Hydraulic machines are devices that convert hydraulic energy into mechanical energy. They are used in a variety of applications, including pumps, turbines, and valves. The design and operation of hydraulic machines are governed by the principles of fluid mechanics.

#### Drainage Hydraulics

Drainage hydraulics deals with the study of the flow of water in drains and sewers. It is a crucial aspect of civil engineering, as it deals with the behavior of water in urban areas.

#### 11.2b Bernoulli's Equation

Bernoulli's equation is a fundamental principle in fluid mechanics that describes the conservation of energy principle for flowing fluids. It is named after the Swiss mathematician Daniel Bernoulli, who first formulated the principle in the 18th century.

Bernoulli's equation is based on the principle of conservation of energy, which states that the total energy of a system remains constant if no energy is added or removed from the system. In the case of fluid flow, this principle can be expressed as:

$$
\frac{1}{2}\rho v^2 + \rho gh + p = constant
$$

where $\rho$ is the fluid density, $v$ is the fluid velocity, $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity, $h$ is the height above a reference point, and $p$ is the pressure.

This equation can be used to analyze fluid flow in a variety of situations, including the design of hydraulic systems. However, it is important to note that Bernoulli's equation assumes that the fluid flow is steady, incompressible, and inviscid. In reality, most fluid flows are not perfectly steady, and the effects of viscosity and compressibility cannot be ignored. Therefore, while Bernoulli's equation is a useful tool, it should be used with caution and supplemented with more advanced analyses when necessary.

#### 11.2c Applications of Fluid Mechanics

Fluid mechanics has a wide range of applications in civil engineering. It is used in the design and analysis of hydraulic systems, including dams, bridges, and canals. It is also used in the design of pipelines, which are used to transport fluids over long distances.

One of the key applications of fluid mechanics in civil engineering is in the design of hydraulic structures. These structures, such as dams and spillways, are designed to control the flow of water. The design of these structures involves a detailed understanding of fluid mechanics, including the principles of fluid dynamics and Bernoulli's equation.

Fluid mechanics is also used in the design of hydraulic machines, such as pumps and turbines. These machines are used to convert hydraulic energy into mechanical energy, and their design involves a detailed understanding of fluid flow and the principles of fluid mechanics.

In addition to these applications, fluid mechanics is also used in the study of sediment transport in rivers and the design of drainage systems. It is also used in the design of hydraulic models, which are used to study the behavior of hydraulic systems under different conditions.

In conclusion, fluid mechanics is a fundamental aspect of civil engineering, with applications in a wide range of areas. A thorough understanding of fluid mechanics is essential for any civil engineer, and it is a key component of the study of civil engineering hydraulics.




### Section: 11.2 Fluid Mechanics:

Fluid mechanics is a fundamental aspect of civil engineering, dealing with the study and application of fluid mechanics to the design and analysis of hydraulic systems. It is a branch of fluid mechanics that deals with the study of fluids in motion, particularly water and its effects on man-made structures such as dams, bridges, and canals.

#### 11.2b Principles of Fluid Mechanics

The principles of fluid mechanics are based on the fundamental laws of physics, including the laws of conservation of mass, momentum, and energy. These principles are used to describe the behavior of fluids in various situations, from the flow of water in a pipe to the movement of air around a building.

#### Conservation of Mass

The principle of conservation of mass, also known as the continuity equation, states that the mass of a fluid element remains constant as it moves through a system. Mathematically, this can be expressed as:

$$
\rho_1 A_1 v_1 = \rho_2 A_2 v_2
$$

where $\rho$ is the density of the fluid, $A$ is the cross-sectional area, and $v$ is the velocity. This equation is used to analyze the flow of fluids in pipes and channels.

#### Conservation of Momentum

The principle of conservation of momentum, also known as the momentum equation, states that the total momentum of a fluid element remains constant unless acted upon by an external force. Mathematically, this can be expressed as:

$$
\rho_1 A_1 v_1 = \rho_2 A_2 v_2
$$

where $F$ is the external force, $A$ is the cross-sectional area, and $v$ is the velocity. This equation is used to analyze the forces acting on fluids in various situations, such as the flow of water over a dam.

#### Conservation of Energy

The principle of conservation of energy, also known as the energy equation, states that the total energy of a fluid element remains constant unless acted upon by an external force. Mathematically, this can be expressed as:

$$
\rho_1 A_1 v_1 = \rho_2 A_2 v_2
$$

where $E$ is the external energy, $A$ is the cross-sectional area, and $v$ is the velocity. This equation is used to analyze the energy changes in fluids, such as the energy losses in a pipe due to friction.

#### Bernoulli's Equation

Bernoulli's equation is a fundamental principle in fluid mechanics that describes the relationship between pressure, velocity, and elevation in a fluid flow. It is derived from the principles of conservation of energy and can be expressed as:

$$
\rho_1 A_1 v_1 = \rho_2 A_2 v_2
$$

where $P$ is the pressure, $h$ is the height, and $v$ is the velocity. This equation is used to analyze the flow of fluids in open channels, such as rivers and canals.

#### Navier-Stokes Equations

The Navier-Stokes equations are a set of nonlinear partial differential equations that describe the motion of viscous fluid substances. They are derived from the principles of conservation of mass, momentum, and energy, and are used to analyze the flow of fluids in various situations, from the flow of blood in the human body to the flow of air around a building.

#### Laminar and Turbulent Flow

Fluid flow can be classified into two types: laminar and turbulent. Laminar flow is smooth and orderly, while turbulent flow is chaotic and disordered. The type of flow can greatly affect the design and operation of hydraulic systems. For example, laminar flow is desirable in pipelines to minimize energy losses, while turbulent flow is necessary in open channels to transport sediment.

#### Viscous Flow

Viscous flow refers to the deformation of a fluid under a shear force, as described by Pascal's law. Ideal fluid, on the other hand, does not deform and follows Bernoulli's equation along streamlines. The behavior of real fluids, which have viscosity and do not follow the principles of ideal fluid flow, is described by the Navier-Stokes equations.

#### Ideal Fluid Flow

Ideal fluid flow is a hypothetical type of fluid flow that assumes no viscosity and no energy losses. It follows Bernoulli's equation along streamlines. Ideal fluid flow is used as a simplification in many fluid mechanics problems, but it is not applicable to real fluids.

#### Real Fluid Flow

Real fluid flow is the actual flow of fluids in various situations. It is affected by viscosity, energy losses, and other factors. The behavior of real fluids is described by the Navier-Stokes equations, which take into account the effects of viscosity and energy losses.

#### Applications of Fluid Mechanics

The principles of fluid mechanics are applied in a wide range of civil engineering problems, from the design of hydraulic structures to the analysis of air flow around buildings. Some common applications include the design of dams, bridges, and canals, the analysis of water supply systems, and the design of HVAC systems for buildings.




### Section: 11.2c Applications of Fluid Mechanics

Fluid mechanics has a wide range of applications in civil engineering. In this section, we will explore some of these applications, including the design of hydraulic systems, the analysis of fluid flow in pipes and channels, and the prediction of flood and wave patterns.

#### Hydraulic Systems

Hydraulic systems are used in a variety of civil engineering applications, from the operation of hydraulic lifts and brakes to the control of water flow in dams and canals. The principles of fluid mechanics are used to design these systems, taking into account the properties of the fluid, the geometry of the system, and the forces acting on the fluid.

For example, the principle of conservation of mass is used to ensure that the volume of fluid entering a system is equal to the volume leaving it. The principle of conservation of momentum is used to analyze the forces acting on the fluid, such as the forces exerted by pumps and valves. The principle of conservation of energy is used to predict the energy losses in the system, such as the losses due to friction and turbulence.

#### Flow Analysis

Flow analysis is another important application of fluid mechanics in civil engineering. It involves the study of fluid flow in pipes and channels, and is used to design and optimize hydraulic systems.

The principle of conservation of mass is used to analyze the flow rate of the fluid, and to ensure that the fluid is evenly distributed throughout the system. The principle of conservation of momentum is used to analyze the forces acting on the fluid, such as the forces exerted by bends and fittings. The principle of conservation of energy is used to predict the energy losses in the system, such as the losses due to friction and turbulence.

#### Flood and Wave Prediction

Flood and wave prediction is a critical application of fluid mechanics in civil engineering. It involves the prediction of flood and wave patterns, which are used to design and optimize flood control systems and coastal defenses.

The principle of conservation of mass is used to analyze the volume of water entering a system, and to ensure that the volume leaving the system is equal to the volume entering it. The principle of conservation of momentum is used to analyze the forces acting on the water, such as the forces exerted by wind and waves. The principle of conservation of energy is used to predict the energy losses in the system, such as the losses due to friction and turbulence.




### Subsection: 11.3a Introduction to Hydrology

Hydrology is a critical aspect of civil engineering, particularly in the design and management of water resources. It is the study of the movement, distribution, and quality of water throughout the Earth. This includes the study of surface water, such as rivers and lakes, as well as groundwater, which is water found beneath the Earth's surface.

#### Water Cycle

The water cycle is a fundamental concept in hydrology. It describes the continuous movement of water on, above, and below the surface of the Earth. The water cycle consists of several processes: evaporation, transpiration, condensation, precipitation, and runoff.

Evaporation is the process by which water changes from a liquid to a gas. This occurs when the sun's heat causes water to evaporate from the surface of the Earth, such as from the oceans, lakes, and rivers.

Transpiration is the process by which water is carried through plants from roots to small pores on the underside of leaves, where it changes to vapor and is released to the atmosphere.

Condensation is the process by which water vapor in the atmosphere cools and changes back into liquid water. This occurs when the water vapor rises into cooler parts of the atmosphere and forms tiny droplets of water.

Precipitation is the process by which water falls to the Earth from the atmosphere. This can occur as rain, snow, sleet, or hail, depending on the temperature and the altitude.

Runoff is the process by which water moves over the surface of the land. This can occur as surface water, such as rivers and lakes, or as groundwater, which seeps into the ground and can travel long distances.

#### Hydrologic Cycle

The hydrologic cycle is a more comprehensive concept than the water cycle. It includes all the processes of the water cycle, but also includes the human use and return of water to the environment. This is particularly important in civil engineering, as human activities can significantly alter the natural water cycle.

The hydrologic cycle can be represented as a closed system, with water constantly moving between the surface of the Earth, the atmosphere, and the ground. However, in reality, there is a small amount of water that is not part of the cycle. This is known as the "freshwater lens," and it is estimated to be about 2.8 million cubic kilometers.

#### Hydrologic Systems

Hydrologic systems are the physical systems that make up the hydrologic cycle. These include rivers, lakes, wetlands, and groundwater systems. Each of these systems plays a unique role in the overall water cycle.

Rivers are the primary means of surface water transport. They carry water from land to the sea, and they are a critical source of freshwater for human use.

Lakes are bodies of water that are typically landlocked. They can be formed by various processes, including tectonic activity, glacial activity, and human activities such as dam construction.

Wetlands are areas of land where the water table is at or near the surface. They are important habitats for a variety of plant and animal species, and they play a crucial role in the water cycle by storing and filtering water.

Groundwater systems are the underground water resources that are found beneath the Earth's surface. They are a critical source of freshwater for human use, particularly in areas where surface water is scarce.

In the following sections, we will delve deeper into each of these hydrologic systems, exploring their characteristics, functions, and the role they play in the overall hydrologic cycle.
